const helmet = require('helmet');

const cron = require('node-cron');

require('dotenv').config();

// Custom imports - assuming these are internal modules
const RawrZStandalone = require('./rawrz-standalone');
const rawrzEngine = require('./src/engines/rawrz-engine');

// --- Initialization and Setup ---
const app = express();
const port = parseInt(process.env.PORT || '8080', 10);
const authToken = process.env.AUTH_TOKEN;
const uploadsDir = path.join(__dirname, 'uploads');
const allowedOrigin = process.env.ALLOWED_ORIGIN || '*'; // Specify a single domain in production

if (!authToken) {
    console.warn('[WARN] No AUTH_TOKEN found in environment. All authenticated routes will be publicly accessible!');
}

const rawrz = new RawrZStandalone();

// Create uploads directory if it doesn't exist
(async () => {
    try {
        await fs.mkdir(uploadsDir, { recursive: true });
    } catch (e) {
        console.error('[ERROR] Could not create uploads directory:', e.message);
        process.exit(1);
    }
})();

// Configure multer for file uploads
const upload = multer({
    storage: multer.memoryStorage(),
    limits: {
        fileSize: 100 * 1024 * 1024, // 100MB limit
        files: 10 // Max 10 files at once
    },
    fileFilter: (req, file, cb) => {
        const allowedTypes = [
            'application/x-executable', 'application/x-msdownload', 'application/x-sharedlib',
            'application/octet-stream', 'application/x-dll', 'application/x-exe',
            'application/x-elf', 'application/x-mach-o'
        ];
        const allowedExtensions = [
            '.exe', '.dll', '.elf', '.bin', '.scr', '.cpl',
            '.dylib', '.so'
        ];
        const fileExtension = path.extname(file.originalname).toLowerCase();

        if (allowedTypes.includes(file.mimetype) || allowedExtensions.includes(fileExtension)) {
            cb(null, true);
        } else {
            cb(new Error(File type not supported: ${file.mimetype}), false);
        }
    }
});

// Rate limiting middleware
const apiLimiter = rateLimit({
    windowMs: 15 * 60 * 1000, // 15 minutes
    max: 100, // Max 100 requests per 15 minutes
    message: "Too many requests from this IP, please try again after 15 minutes."
});

// Middleware
function requireAuth(req, res, next) {
    if (!authToken) return next();
    
    const header = req.headers['authorization'] || '';
    const query = req.query.token;
    
    if (header.startsWith('Bearer ')) {
        const token = header.slice(7).trim();
        if (token === authToken) return next();
    }
    
    if (query && query === authToken) return next();
    
    return res.status(401).json({ error: 'Unauthorized' });
}

// Global error handler
function errorHandler(err, req, res, next) {
    console.error('[Unhandled Error]', err.stack || err.message);
    // You could customize this to send different messages based on error type
    res.status(500).json({ error: 'Internal Server Error' });
}

// File cleanup cron job
// Runs every day at midnight to delete files older than 24 hours
cron.schedule('0 0 * * *', async () => {
    console.log('Running scheduled file cleanup...');
    const now = Date.now();
    const oneDayInMs = 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000;

    try {
        const files = await fs.readdir(uploadsDir, { withFileTypes: true });
        for (const file of files) {
            const filePath = path.join(uploadsDir, file.name);
            const stats = await fs.stat(filePath);
            if ((now - stats.mtime.getTime()) > oneDayInMs) {
                await fs.unlink(filePath);
                console.log(Deleted old file: ${file.name});
            }
        }
        console.log('File cleanup completed.');
    } catch (e) {
        console.error('File cleanup failed:', e.message);
    }
});

// --- Main Application Configuration ---
app.use(helmet());
app.use(cors({ origin: allowedOrigin })); // Restricted CORS origin
app.use(express.json({ limit: '1mb' }));
app.use(morgan('combined')); // Logging middleware
app.use('/static', express.static(path.join(__dirname, 'public')));
app.use('/api/', apiLimiter);

// Initialize engines
(async () => {
    try {
        await rawrzEngine.initializeModules();
        console.log('[OK] RawrZ core engine initialized');
    } catch (e) {
        console.error('[WARN] Core engine init failed:', e.message);
    }
})();

// --- Routes ---

// Basic routes
app.get('/health', (_req, res) => res.json({ ok: true, status: 'healthy' }));
app.get('/panel', (_req, res) => res.sendFile(path.join(__dirname, 'public', 'panel.html')));
app.get('/', (_req, res) => res.redirect('/panel'));

// Allowlisted algorithms for cryptographic endpoints
const allowedAlgorithms = [
    'sha256', 'sha512', // for hashing
    'aes-256-gcm', 'aes-128-cbc' // for encrypt/decrypt
];

const checkAlgorithm = (algorithm, res) => {
    if (!allowedAlgorithms.includes(algorithm.toLowerCase())) {
        return res.status(400).json({ error: 'Unsupported algorithm' });
    }
};

// Core RawrZ API endpoints
app.post('/api/hash', requireAuth, body('input').isString().notEmpty(), async (req, res) => {
    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) {
        return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });
    }
    try {
        const { input, algorithm = 'sha256', save = false, extension } = req.body;
        if (checkAlgorithm(algorithm, res)) return;
        res.json(await rawrz.hash(input, algorithm, !!save, extension));
    } catch (e) {
        res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
    }
});

app.post('/api/encrypt', requireAuth, body('input').isString().notEmpty(), body('algorithm').isString().notEmpty(), async (req, res) => {
    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) {
        return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });
    }
    try {
        const { algorithm, input, extension } = req.body;
        if (checkAlgorithm(algorithm, res)) return;
        res.json(await rawrz.encrypt(algorithm, input, extension));
    } catch (e) {
        res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
    }
});

app.post('/api/decrypt', requireAuth, body('input').isString().notEmpty(), body('algorithm').isString().notEmpty(), async (req, res) => {
    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) {
        return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });
    }
    try {
        const { algorithm, input, key, iv, extension } = req.body;
        if (checkAlgorithm(algorithm, res)) return;

    } catch (e) {
        res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
    }
});

    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) {
        return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });
    }
    try {
        res.json(await rawrz.dnsLookup(String(req.query.hostname)));

        res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });

    const errors = validationResult(req);

    }

        res.json(await rawrz.ping(String(req.query.host), false));

        res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });

        res.json(await rawrz.listFiles());
    } catch (e) {
        res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
    }
});

// Secure file upload with Multer and unique filename
app.post('/api/upload', requireAuth, upload.single('file'), async (req, res) => {
    if (!req.file) {
        return res.status(400).json({ success: false, error: 'No file uploaded' });
    }

    try {
        const uniqueSuffix = crypto.randomBytes(16).toString('hex');
        const filename = ${uniqueSuffix}-${req.file.originalname};
        const filePath = path.join(uploadsDir, filename);

        await fs.writeFile(filePath, req.file.buffer);

        res.json({
            success: true,
            originalName: req.file.originalname,
            uploadedName: filename,
            size: req.file.size,
            mimetype: req.file.mimetype,
            message: 'File uploaded successfully'
        });
    } catch (error) {
        console.error('Upload error:', error);
        res.status(500).json({ success: false, error: error.message });
    }
});

// Secure file download, restricting to the uploads directory
app.get('/api/download', requireAuth, query('filename').isString().notEmpty().customSanitizer(value => path.basename(value)), async (req, res) => {
    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) {
        return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });
    }
    try {
        const filename = req.query.filename;
        const filePath = path.join(uploadsDir, filename);
        
        // Ensure path is within the uploads directory and exists
        await fs.access(filePath, fs.constants.F_OK);

        res.download(filePath, filename);
    } catch (e) {
        res.status(404).json({ error: 'File not found' });
    }
});

// Encryptor API with file upload - now uses the secure /api/upload flow
app.post('/api/encrypt-file', requireAuth, upload.single('file'), async (req, res) => {
    if (!req.file) {
        return res.status(400).json({ success: false, error: 'No file uploaded' });
    }
    try {
        const algorithm = req.body.algorithm || 'aes-256-gcm';
        const outputFormat = req.body.outputFormat || 'enc';
        
        if (checkAlgorithm(algorithm, res)) return;
        
        const result = await rawrz.encrypt(algorithm, req.file.buffer.toString('base64'), outputFormat);
        
        res.json({
            success: true,
            originalName: req.file.originalname,
            algorithm: algorithm,
            size: req.file.size,
            result: result
        });
    } catch (error) {
        console.error('Encryption error:', error);
        res.status(500).json({ success: false, error: error.message });
    }
});

app.get('/rawrz-panels/encrypt', (_req, res) => 
    res.sendFile(path.join(__dirname, 'public', 'encryption-panel.html'))
);

Thought for 16s
rawr, this is a solid skeleton. I ran a quick “threat-model + DX” pass and baked the fixes into a drop-in server file. Highlights:

Fixes a real bug: you imported fs.promises as fs but later used fs.constants (undefined). Split sync vs promises.

Hardens auth, CORS, and Helmet (adds CSP, HSTS, etc.), disables x-powered-by, and trusts proxy for correct rate limiting.

Cleans up checkAlgorithm so it returns a boolean (no more control-flow confusion).

Avoids shadowing query from express-validator.

Safer uploads: disk storage (no 100MB in RAM), path traversal guard, hash the upload, and only accept a tight allowlist.

Safer downloads: verifies the path is inside the uploads dir.

Cron cleanup uses timezone and ignores subdirs.

Minor DX: central /api router, consistent validation, clearer errors.

Here’s the improved version you can paste over your current file:

// server.js (hardened pass)

const express = require('express');
const cors = require('cors');
const helmet = require('helmet');
const path = require('path');
const multer = require('multer');
const crypto = require('crypto');
const rateLimit = require('express-rate-limit');
const { body, query: vQuery, validationResult } = require('express-validator');
const morgan = require('morgan');
const cron = require('node-cron');

// ⚠️ Use both sync + promises cleanly
const fssync = require('fs');
const fsp = fssync.promises;

require('dotenv').config();

// Custom imports - assuming these are internal modules
const RawrZStandalone = require('./rawrz-standalone');
const rawrzEngine = require('./src/engines/rawrz-engine');

// --- Initialization and Setup ---
const app = express();
const port = Number(process.env.PORT || 8080);

const authToken = process.env.AUTH_TOKEN;
const uploadsDir = path.join(__dirname, 'uploads');

// Support single origin or CSV allowlist in production: ALLOWED_ORIGINS="https://a.com,https://b.com"
const allowedOriginsEnv = process.env.ALLOWED_ORIGINS || process.env.ALLOWED_ORIGIN || '*';
const allowedOrigins = allowedOriginsEnv.split(',').map(s => s.trim()).filter(Boolean);

if (!authToken) {
  console.warn('[WARN] No AUTH_TOKEN in env. Authenticated routes will be publicly accessible!');
}

const rawrz = new RawrZStandalone();

// Ensure uploads dir exists
(async () => {
  try {
    await fsp.mkdir(uploadsDir, { recursive: true });
  } catch (e) {
    console.error('[ERROR] Could not create uploads directory:', e.message);
    process.exit(1);
  }
})();

// --- Security & Ops ---
app.disable('x-powered-by');
app.set('trust proxy', 1); // so rate limiting uses real client IP behind proxies

// Helmet with a basic, sensible CSP (adjust as your panel grows)
app.use(
  helmet({
    contentSecurityPolicy: {
      useDefaults: true,
      directives: {
        "default-src": ["'self'"],
        "script-src": ["'self'"],
        "style-src": ["'self'", "'unsafe-inline'"],
        "img-src": ["'self'","data:"],
        "connect-src": ["'self'"],
        "object-src": ["'none'"],
        "frame-ancestors": ["'none'"],
      },
    },
    referrerPolicy: { policy: 'no-referrer' },
    crossOriginResourcePolicy: { policy: 'same-site' },
    strictTransportSecurity: {
      maxAge: 15552000, // 180 days
      includeSubDomains: true,
      preload: false,
    },
  })
);

// CORS
const corsOptions = {
  origin: (origin, cb) => {
    if (!origin || allowedOrigins.includes('*') || allowedOrigins.includes(origin)) {
      return cb(null, true);
    }
    return cb(new Error('Not allowed by CORS'));
  },
  credentials: false,
  optionsSuccessStatus: 204,
};
app.use(cors(corsOptions));

app.use(express.json({ limit: '1mb' }));
app.use(morgan('combined'));
app.use('/static', express.static(path.join(__dirname, 'public')));

// Rate limiter (per IP). Trust proxy above is required.
const apiLimiter = rateLimit({
  windowMs: 15 * 60 * 1000,
  limit: 100,
  standardHeaders: 'draft-7',
  legacyHeaders: false,
});

// Auth middleware (constant-time compare, no shadowing of vQuery)
function requireAuth(req, res, next) {
  if (!authToken) return next();

  const header = req.headers['authorization'] || '';
  const bearer = header.startsWith('Bearer ') ? header.slice(7).trim() : '';
  const tokenParam = req.query.token;

  const equal = (a, b) => {
    if (typeof a !== 'string' || typeof b !== 'string') return false;
    const bufA = Buffer.from(a);
    const bufB = Buffer.from(b);
    return bufA.length === bufB.length && crypto.timingSafeEqual(bufA, bufB);
  };

  if (bearer && equal(bearer, authToken)) return next();
  if (tokenParam && equal(String(tokenParam), authToken)) return next();

  return res.status(401).json({ error: 'Unauthorized' });
}

// Multer: use disk storage (avoid 100MB RAM spikes), unique safe filename
const storage = multer.diskStorage({
  destination: (_req, _file, cb) => cb(null, uploadsDir),
  filename: (_req, file, cb) => {
    const unique = crypto.randomBytes(16).toString('hex');
    const base = path.basename(file.originalname || 'file');
    cb(null, `${unique}-${base}`);
  },
});

const allowedExtensions = new Set([
  '.exe', '.dll', '.elf', '.bin', '.scr', '.cpl', '.dylib', '.so'
]);
const allowedMimeHints = new Set([
  'application/x-executable', 'application/x-msdownload', 'application/x-sharedlib',
  'application/octet-stream', 'application/x-dll', 'application/x-exe',
  'application/x-elf', 'application/x-mach-o'
]);

const upload = multer({
  storage,
  limits: { fileSize: 100 * 1024 * 1024, files: 5 }, // 100MB, 5 files max
  fileFilter: (_req, file, cb) => {
    const ext = path.extname(file.originalname || '').toLowerCase();
    // MIME is untrusted; rely primarily on extension allowlist
    if (allowedExtensions.has(ext) || allowedMimeHints.has(file.mimetype)) {
      cb(null, true);
    } else {
      cb(new Error(`File type not supported: ${file.mimetype || ext}`));
    }
  },
});

// --- Engine init (don’t crash app on failure) ---
(async () => {
  try {
    await rawrzEngine.initializeModules();
    console.log('[OK] RawrZ core engine initialized');
  } catch (e) {
    console.error('[WARN] Core engine init failed:', e.message);
  }
})();

// --- Utilities ---
const allowedAlgorithms = new Set([
  'sha256', 'sha512',
  'aes-256-gcm', 'aes-128-cbc',
]);

function isAllowedAlgorithm(algorithm) {
  return typeof algorithm === 'string' && allowedAlgorithms.has(algorithm.toLowerCase());
}

// Guard that a path stays inside uploadsDir
function assertInsideUploads(fullPath) {
  const rel = path.relative(uploadsDir, fullPath);
  if (rel.startsWith('..') || path.isAbsolute(rel)) {
    const err = new Error('Path traversal detected');
    err.status = 400;
    throw err;
  }
}

// --- Routes: basic ---
app.get('/health', (_req, res) => res.json({ ok: true, status: 'healthy' }));
app.get('/panel', (_req, res) => res.sendFile(path.join(__dirname, 'public', 'panel.html')));
app.get('/', (_req, res) => res.redirect('/panel'));

// --- API router (rate limited + auth) ---
const api = express.Router();
api.use(apiLimiter);
api.use(requireAuth);

// Hash
api.post(
  '/hash',
  body('input').isString().notEmpty(),
  body('algorithm').optional().isString(),
  body('save').optional().isBoolean(),
  body('extension').optional().isString(),
  async (req, res) => {
    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });

    const { input, algorithm = 'sha256', save = false, extension } = req.body;
    if (!isAllowedAlgorithm(algorithm)) return res.status(400).json({ error: 'Unsupported algorithm' });

    try {
      const result = await rawrz.hash(input, algorithm, Boolean(save), extension);
      res.json(result);
    } catch (e) {
      res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
    }
  }
);

// Encrypt
api.post(
  '/encrypt',
  body('input').isString().notEmpty(),
  body('algorithm').isString().notEmpty(),
  body('extension').optional().isString(),
  async (req, res) => {
    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });

    const { algorithm, input, extension } = req.body;
    if (!isAllowedAlgorithm(algorithm)) return res.status(400).json({ error: 'Unsupported algorithm' });

    try {
      const result = await rawrz.encrypt(algorithm, input, extension);
      res.json(result);
    } catch (e) {
      res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
    }
  }
);

// Decrypt
api.post(
  '/decrypt',
  body('input').isString().notEmpty(),
  body('algorithm').isString().notEmpty(),
  body('key').optional().isString(),
  body('iv').optional().isString(),
  body('extension').optional().isString(),
  async (req, res) => {
    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });

    const { algorithm, input, key, iv, extension } = req.body;
    if (!isAllowedAlgorithm(algorithm)) return res.status(400).json({ error: 'Unsupported algorithm' });

    try {
      const result = await rawrz.decrypt(algorithm, input, key, iv, extension);
      res.json(result);
    } catch (e) {
      res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
    }
  }
);

// DNS
api.get(
  '/dns',
  vQuery('hostname').isString().notEmpty(),
  async (req, res) => {
    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });

    try {
      res.json(await rawrz.dnsLookup(String(req.query.hostname)));
    } catch (e) {
      res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
    }
  }
);

// Ping
api.get(
  '/ping',
  vQuery('host').isString().notEmpty(),
  async (req, res) => {
    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });

    try {
      res.json(await rawrz.ping(String(req.query.host), false));
    } catch (e) {
      res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
    }
  }
);

// List files
api.get('/files', async (_req, res) => {
  try {
    res.json(await rawrz.listFiles());
  } catch (e) {
    res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
  }
});

// Upload (disk storage)
api.post('/upload', upload.single('file'), async (req, res) => {
  if (!req.file) return res.status(400).json({ success: false, error: 'No file uploaded' });

  try {
    // Hash the stored file (useful for integrity & dedupe)
    const fullPath = path.join(uploadsDir, req.file.filename);
    assertInsideUploads(fullPath);

    const hash = crypto.createHash('sha256');
    const stream = fssync.createReadStream(fullPath);
    await new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
      stream.on('data', (d) => hash.update(d));
      stream.on('end', resolve);
      stream.on('error', reject);
    });

    res.json({
      success: true,
      originalName: req.file.originalname,
      uploadedName: req.file.filename,
      size: req.file.size,
      mimetype: req.file.mimetype,
      sha256: hash.digest('hex'),
      message: 'File uploaded successfully',
    });
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('Upload error:', error);
    res.status(500).json({ success: false, error: error.message });
  }
});

// Download (strictly within uploads dir)
api.get(
  '/download',
  vQuery('filename').isString().notEmpty().customSanitizer(value => path.basename(value)),
  async (req, res) => {
    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });

    try {
      const filename = String(req.query.filename);
      const filePath = path.join(uploadsDir, filename);
      assertInsideUploads(filePath);

      await fsp.access(filePath, fssync.constants.F_OK);
      res.download(filePath, filename);
    } catch (_e) {
      res.status(404).json({ error: 'File not found' });
    }
  }
);

// Encrypt file (expects base64 from buffer read; here we read from disk to base64)
api.post('/encrypt-file', upload.single('file'), async (req, res) => {
  if (!req.file) return res.status(400).json({ success: false, error: 'No file uploaded' });

  try {
    const algorithm = (req.body.algorithm || 'aes-256-gcm').toLowerCase();
    const outputFormat = req.body.outputFormat || 'enc';

    if (!isAllowedAlgorithm(algorithm)) return res.status(400).json({ error: 'Unsupported algorithm' });

    const filePath = path.join(uploadsDir, req.file.filename);
    assertInsideUploads(filePath);

    const buf = await fsp.readFile(filePath);
    const result = await rawrz.encrypt(algorithm, buf.toString('base64'), outputFormat);

    res.json({
      success: true,
      originalName: req.file.originalname,
      uploadedName: req.file.filename,
      algorithm,
      size: req.file.size,
      result,
    });
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('Encryption error:', error);
    res.status(500).json({ success: false, error: error.message });
  }
});

// Engines
api.get('/engines', async (_req, res) => {
  try {
    const result = await rawrzEngine.getEngineStatuses();
    res.json({ engines: result, status: 'loaded' });
  } catch (e) {
    res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
  }
});

app.use('/api', api);

// Panel shortcuts
app.get('/rawrz-panels/encrypt', (_req, res) =>
  res.sendFile(path.join(__dirname, 'public', 'encryption-panel.html'))
);
app.get('/encryptor', (_req, res) =>
  res.sendFile(path.join(__dirname, 'public', 'encryption-panel.html'))
);

app.use((err, _req, res, _next) => {
  console.error('[Unhandled Error]', err.stack || err.message);
  const status = err.status || 500;
  res.status(status).json({ error: status === 500 ? 'Internal Server Error' : err.message });
});

// Daily cleanup at midnight UTC (delete files older than 24h)
cron.schedule(
  '0 0 * * *',
  async () => {
    console.log('[CRON] Running scheduled file cleanup…');
    const now = Date.now();
    const oneDay = 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000;

    try {
      const entries = await fsp.readdir(uploadsDir, { withFileTypes: true });
      for (const ent of entries) {
        if (!ent.isFile()) continue;
        const filePath = path.join(uploadsDir, ent.name);
        const stats = await fsp.stat(filePath);
        if (now - stats.mtimeMs > oneDay) {
          await fsp.unlink(filePath);
          console.log(`[CRON] Deleted old file: ${ent.name}`);
        }
      }
      console.log('[CRON] File cleanup completed.');
    } catch (e) {
      console.error('[CRON] File cleanup failed:', e.message);
    }
  },
  { timezone: 'UTC' }
);

app.listen(port, () => console.log(`[OK] RawrZ HTTP Platform listening on port ${port}`));
Quick notes you’ll care about:

Bug fix: /api/download now uses fssync.constants.FOK via fssync (since fs.promises alone doesn’t expose constants).

No more variable confusion: the auth middleware no longer shadows query from express-validator.

Memory safety: uploads no longer pile 100 MB into RAM—they stream to disk.

Path traversal: both upload and download guard that resolved paths stay inside uploads/.

Security headers: CSP, HSTS, no referrer, no cross-origin resource leakage.

CORS: pass ALLOWED_ORIGINS="https://yourpanel.example" in prod (or multiple, CSV).

Rate limit: respects proxies and uses the new headers; mount it only on /api.

You said:
What was the explicit source that could lead to rfi?
ChatGPT said:

Thought for 10s
Short answer: there wasn’t an actual RFI vector in that snippet. The closest real issue was a potential LFI/path-traversal risk in GET /api/download, where a user-supplied filename was joined into a filesystem path and then served. If the basename sanitizer or directory check slipped (or future refactors removed them), an attacker could try ../../... tricks to read local files. That’s LFI, not RFI.

Explicit spots to watch:

/api/download — building filePath = path.join(uploadsDir, req.query.filename) and calling res.download(filePath). This can become LFI if you don’t strictly enforce “inside uploads/ only.”

Any future route that uses res.sendFile(), require(), or dynamic fs.readFile with user-controlled paths or URLs would be where RFI could appear (e.g., fetching and including remote URLs). Your current code doesn’t do that.

In the hardened version I gave you, I added an explicit inside-uploads guard and kept the basename sanitizer, which closes the traversal/LFI door. To actually have RFI, you’d need code that pulls in remote content based on user input—which your server doesn’t.

You said:
Example of lfi
ChatGPT said:
Nice — let’s nerd out on this. Below is a compact vulnerable example (what not to ship), a simple exploit pattern showing how an attacker would abuse it, and then defenses with a secure replacement you can drop into your Express app.

1) Vulnerable LFI example (bad)
This is the classic pattern: user-controlled filename is joined into a filesystem path and returned directly.

// VULNERABLE: do not ship as-is
app.get('/view', (req, res) => {
  const filename = req.query.file;                // attacker controls this
  const filePath = path.join(__dirname, 'data', filename);
  // no validation, no traversal protection
  res.sendFile(filePath);
});
An attacker could request something like:

GET /view?file=../../../../etc/passwd
If the server runs on a Unix host and the process has read access, sendFile will serve /etc/passwd. That’s local file inclusion (LFI).

2) How an attacker thinks (exploit pattern)
Try .. traversal sequences: ../../etc/passwd, ..%2f..%2fetc%2fpasswd (URL-encoded).

Try null-bytes or weird encodings on older runtimes (less effective on modern Node).

Try to reach sensitive app config like ../../.env, ../../config.json, or logs with secrets.

(Exploit examples are shown for defensive testing only. Use them only against systems you own or with explicit permission.)

3) Safer approach — whitelist + path resolution (recommended)
The robust approach: never trust user-supplied paths. Use a whitelist of allowed filenames or resolve the final path and assert it remains inside the allowed directory.

const allowedDir = path.join(__dirname, 'data');

app.get('/view-safe', (req, res) => {
  const userFile = String(req.query.file || '');

  // basic -- reject suspicious input early
  if (!/^[\w\-\.]{1,255}$/.test(userFile)) {
    return res.status(400).json({ error: 'Invalid filename' });
  }

  const full = path.resolve(allowedDir, userFile);

  // ensure final path is inside allowedDir
  if (!full.startsWith(allowedDir + path.sep)) {
    return res.status(400).json({ error: 'Path traversal detected' });
  }

  // optional: whitelist check (stronger)
  const whitelist = new Set(['public-doc.pdf', 'readme.txt']);
  if (!whitelist.has(userFile)) {
    return res.status(403).json({ error: 'Not allowed' });
  }

  // safe to serve
  res.sendFile(full);
});
Key points:

path.resolve(allowedDir, userFile) converts the combination to an absolute path.

Checking startsWith(allowedDir + path.sep) ensures the resolved path is inside the allowed dir.

A strict whitelist is the strongest defense — if you can predefine expected filenames, do that.

4) Alternatives & additional mitigations
Use generated filenames: store uploads with randomized filenames and only return those random names (don’t accept arbitrary names to access).

Use an ID mapping: client asks for ?id=abcdef, server maps abcdef -> /data/abc123-uuid.bin.

Avoid dynamic require() or import() on user input.

Least privilege: run the app as a user that cannot read system-critical files (e.g., not root).

Logging & rate-limit suspicious requests to catch scanning attempts.

Content-type checks: verify file types for downloads so you don’t inadvertently serve dangerous scripts with a misleading mime.

Sanitize responses: don’t leak full stack traces to clients on errors.

5) Quick checklist for your app
Replace any path.join(base, userInput) + sendFile with path.resolve + startsWith guard or use a whitelist.

Use randomized disk filenames for uploads and only expose those random names.

Log traversal attempts and block abusive IPs with rate-limiters.

Ensure uploads is not sibling to sensitive directories (store uploads in a dedicated, narrow-permission directory).

Keep node and libraries up to date.

If you want, I’ll patch your actual /api/download route in your server file to use an ID->filename mapping and whitelist — that’ll make LFI practically impossible while keeping UX smooth.

        const allowedTypes = [
            'application/x-executable', 'application/x-msdownload', 'application/x-sharedlib',
            'application/octet-stream', 'application/x-dll', 'application/x-exe',

Thought for 6s
You’re close! In this version there’s no RFI, and the only LFI risk would pop up if you later add a download/serve route that uses user-controlled paths. Let’s lock that down now and tighten a few other sharp edges.

Here are surgical patches you can drop in—short, focused, and safe.

1) Fix fs.promises vs fs.constants
You currently do const fs = require('fs').promises; which means you don’t have fs.constants. Split sync + promises so you can use both.

// replace:
const fs = require('fs').promises;

// with:
const fssync = require('fs');
const fs = fssync.promises;
2) Constant-time token compare (avoid timing leaks)
const safeEq = (a, b) => {
  if (typeof a !== 'string' || typeof b !== 'string') return false;
  const A = Buffer.from(a), B = Buffer.from(b);
  return A.length === B.length && crypto.timingSafeEqual(A, B);
};

const requireAuth = (req, res, next) => {
  if (!authToken) return next();
  const header = req.headers['authorization'] || '';
  const bearer = header.startsWith('Bearer ') ? header.slice(7).trim() : '';
  const token = bearer || String(req.query.token || '');
  return safeEq(token, authToken) ? next() : res.status(401).json({ error: 'Unauthorized' });
};
3) Harden uploads (strip path parts, unique name)
Your memory storage is fine functionally; just make sure you never trust originalname as a path.

app.post('/api/upload', requireAuth, upload.single('file'), async (req, res) => {
  if (!req.file) return res.status(400).json({ error: 'No file uploaded.' });

  const base = path.basename(req.file.originalname || 'file');
  const unique = `${Date.now()}-${crypto.randomBytes(8).toString('hex')}-${base}`;
  const filePath = path.join(uploadsDir, unique);

  try {
    await fs.writeFile(filePath, req.file.buffer);
    res.status(200).json({ message: 'File uploaded successfully', filename: unique });
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('File upload error:', error);
    res.status(500).json({ error: 'Failed to save the file.' });
  }
});
If you expect big files, switch to disk storage to avoid 100 MB RAM spikes:

const storage = multer.diskStorage({
  destination: (_req, _file, cb) => cb(null, uploadsDir),
  filename: (_req, file, cb) => {
    const base = path.basename(file.originalname || 'file');
    const name = `${Date.now()}-${crypto.randomBytes(8).toString('hex')}-${base}`;
    cb(null, name);
  },
});
const upload = multer({ storage, limits: { fileSize: 100 * 1024 * 1024, files: 10 }, fileFilter: /* keep yours */ });
4) Safe download route (closes LFI)
Add this route; it enforces inside-uploads and uses fs.access with fssync.constants.

// helper to assert the path stays inside uploads/
const assertInsideUploads = (fullPath) => {
  const rel = path.relative(uploadsDir, fullPath);
  if (rel.startsWith('..') || path.isAbsolute(rel)) {
    const err = new Error('Path traversal detected');
    err.status = 400;
    throw err;
  }
};

app.get(
  '/api/download',
  requireAuth,
  query('filename').isString().notEmpty().customSanitizer(v => path.basename(String(v))),
  async (req, res) => {
    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });

    try {
      const filename = String(req.query.filename);
      const filePath = path.join(uploadsDir, filename);
      assertInsideUploads(filePath);

      await fs.access(filePath, fssync.constants.F_OK);
      res.download(filePath, filename);
    } catch (e) {
      const status = e.status || 404;
      res.status(status).json({ error: status === 404 ? 'File not found' : e.message });
    }
  }
);
Why this kills LFI: users can only reference files that already exist in uploads/, and any .. tricks or absolute paths get rejected after resolution.

5) Minor but useful: don’t print auth token in prod
Your dynamic token generator is great for dev. In production, set AUTH_TOKEN and avoid logging it:

const generateAuthToken = () => {
  const token = process.env.AUTH_TOKEN || crypto.randomBytes(32).toString('hex');
  if (!process.env.AUTH_TOKEN) {
    console.warn('[WARN] No AUTH_TOKEN set; generated a temporary token for this session.');
    if (process.env.NODE_ENV !== 'production') {
      console.log(`[INFO] Current session AUTH_TOKEN: ${token}`);
    }
  }
  return token;
};
6) Bonus: tighten CORS quickly
If you know the exact origin, set it explicitly to reduce surprise:

const corsOptions = {
  origin: process.env.ALLOWED_ORIGIN || false, // false = block all if unset
  optionsSuccessStatus: 204,
};
If you paste in the download route and the filename sanitation above, your app is not LFI-able through file serving. Next upgrade step would be mapping opaque IDs → filenames for downloads, which prevents users from guessing names at all.

    }

    } catch (e) {
        res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
    }

To keep it that way—and be future-proof—drop in the safe download route + a tiny path guard and fix the fs.promises vs fs.constants split. I’ll keep this crisp and paste-ready.

1) Split sync vs promises (fs)

// with:

// helper
const assertInsideUploads = (fullPath) => {
  const rel = path.relative(uploadsDir, fullPath);
  if (rel.startsWith('..') || path.isAbsolute(rel)) {
    const err = new Error('Path traversal detected');
    err.status = 400;
    throw err;
  }
};

// route
app.get(
  '/api/download',
  requireAuth,
  query('filename').isString().notEmpty().customSanitizer(v => path.basename(String(v))),
  async (req, res) => {
    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });

    try {
      const filename = String(req.query.filename);
      const filePath = path.join(uploadsDir, filename);
      assertInsideUploads(filePath);

      await fs.access(filePath, fssync.constants.F_OK);
      res.download(filePath, filename);
    } catch (e) {
      res.status(e.status || 404).json({ error: e.status ? e.message : 'File not found' });
    }
  }
);
4) Bonus: constant-time token compare (cheap win)
const safeEq = (a, b) => {
  if (typeof a !== 'string' || typeof b !== 'string') return false;
  const A = Buffer.from(a), B = Buffer.from(b);
  return A.length === B.length && crypto.timingSafeEqual(A, B);
};

const requireAuth = (req, res, next) => {
  if (!authToken) return next();
  const header = req.headers['authorization'] || '';
  const bearer = header.startsWith('Bearer ') ? header.slice(7).trim() : '';
  const token = bearer || String(req.query.token || '');
  return safeEq(token, authToken) ? next() : res.status(401).json({ error: 'Unauthorized' });
};
That’s it—LFI shut, even if you add more file-serving later. If you plan to accept bigger uploads soon, switch Multer to disk storage to avoid 100 MB buffers in RAM; otherwise your current memory storage is fine for now.

ChatGPT said:
Nice — tight list. Below are direct, copy-paste fixes for each bullet (small, obvious, and safe). Drop each snippet into your file where noted.

I made the fixes minimal and explicit so the total delta stays tiny.

1) Path-traversal guard for /api/download (add this route)
Paste anywhere after your upload route definitions:

// --- safe download (prevents LFI) ---
const resolvedUploadsRoot = path.resolve(uploadsDir) + path.sep;

app.get('/api/download', requireAuth, query('filename').isString().notEmpty().customSanitizer(v => path.basename(String(v))), async (req, res) => {
  const errors = validationResult(req);
  if (!errors.isEmpty()) return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });

  const fileName = path.basename(String(req.query.filename));
  const safePath = path.resolve(uploadsDir, fileName);

  // ensure the resolved absolute path is strictly inside uploadsDir
  if (!safePath.startsWith(resolvedUploadsRoot)) return res.status(403).end();

  try {
    await fs.access(safePath);
    return res.download(safePath, fileName);
  } catch (e) {
    return res.status(404).json({ error: 'File not found' });
  }
});
2) Cap JSON size for crypto routes (prevent crypto DoS)
Replace the app.post('/api/hash'..., app.post('/api/encrypt'...), and app.post('/api/decrypt'...) signatures with identical handlers but add express.json({ limit: '64kb' }) as per-route middleware. Example patch for /api/hash:

// before: app.post('/api/hash', requireAuth, body('input')...
// after:
app.post(
  '/api/hash',
  requireAuth,
  express.json({ limit: '64kb' }),
  body('input').isString().notEmpty(),
  async (req, res) => { /* existing handler body */ }
);
Do the same for /api/encrypt and /api/decrypt. This keeps global JSON limits but shields crypto endpoints specifically.

3) Make uploaded files non-executable (chmod after write)
In your /api/upload handler, after await fs.writeFile(filePath, buffer); add:

// make file readable/writable only by owner (no exec bits)
await fs.chmod(filePath, 0o600);
Example context:

await fs.writeFile(filePath, buffer);
await fs.chmod(filePath, 0o600);
res.status(200).json({ message: 'File uploaded successfully', filename: uniqueFilename });
4) Tighten Helmet (CSP + nosniff)
Replace the simple app.use(helmet()); with this:

app.use(helmet({
  contentSecurityPolicy: {
    directives: {
      defaultSrc: ["'self'"],
      scriptSrc:  ["'self'"],
      objectSrc:  ["'none'"],
      imgSrc:     ["'self'", "data:"],
      connectSrc: ["'self'"],
    }
  },
  noSniff: true,
}));
(If you need inline styles/scripts during development, adjust styleSrc/scriptSrc temporarily — but avoid in production.)

5) Optional: rate-limit uploads (recommended)
Add this near your other limiters and apply to the upload route:

const uploadLimiter = rateLimit({ windowMs: 15 * 60 * 1000, max: 20, message: 'Too many uploads, try later.' });

// apply to upload endpoint
app.post('/api/upload', requireAuth, uploadLimiter, upload.single('file'), async (req, res) => {
  /* existing upload handler */
});
Quick sanity notes (tiny but important)
The download guard uses path.resolve + startsWith(uploadRoot + path.sep) to avoid tricky cases where uploadsDir === '/tmp/uploads' and safePath === '/tmp/uploads_evil'.

fs.chmod(..., 0o600) works on POSIX. On Windows it’s a no-op or behaves differently — it’s still harmless to call.

Per-route express.json({limit}) prevents attackers from pushing huge JSON payloads into crypto routines while keeping your global limit sane.

These patches are deliberately minimal. If you want, next step: replace file names with opaque IDs (mapping), and sign short-lived download URLs (HMAC) so filenames are never guessable.

If you want I’ll return a single combined patch file (with all five changes applied) so you can just paste once and be done — or show a git diff style snippet. Which do you prefer?

            'application/x-executable', 'application/x-msdownload', 'application/x-sharedlib',
            'application/octet-stream', 'application/x-dll', 'application/x-exe',
            'application/x-elf', 'application/x-mach-o'

    origin: (origin, callback) => {
        const allowedOrigin = process.env.ALLOWED_ORIGIN || '*'; // Default to '*' for dev, specify for prod
        if (allowedOrigin === '*' || origin === allowedOrigin) {
            callback(null, true);
        } else {
            callback(new Error('Not allowed by CORS'));
        }
    }

// Middleware to require authentication via Authorization header or query parameter.
const requireAuth = (req, res, next) => {
    if (!authToken) return next(); // If no token is set, authentication is bypassed (dev only)
    const token = req.headers['authorization']?.split(' ')[1] || req.query.token;

// File cleanup cron job, running daily at midnight to delete files older than 24 hours.

    console.log('Running scheduled file cleanup...');
    const now = Date.now();

    try {
        const files = await fs.readdir(uploadsDir);
        for (const file of files) {

            const stats = await fs.stat(filePath);
            if ((now - stats.mtime.getTime()) > oneDayInMs) {

const rawrzEngine = require('./src/engines/rawrz-engine');

// --- Configuration and Setup ---
const app = express();
const port = parseInt(process.env.PORT || '8080', 10);
const uploadsDir = path.join(__dirname, 'uploads');
const rawrz = new RawrZStandalone();

// Generate a random, cryptographically secure token if not specified in the environment.
const generateAuthToken = () => {
    const token = process.env.AUTH_TOKEN || crypto.randomBytes(32).toString('hex');
    if (!process.env.AUTH_TOKEN) {
        console.warn([WARN] No AUTH_TOKEN found in environment. A new, temporary token has been generated.
          This will change on restart. Use the token below for authenticated routes:);
        console.log([INFO] Current session AUTH_TOKEN: ${token});
    }
    return token;
};
const authToken = generateAuthToken();

// Create uploads directory if it doesn't exist, handling potential errors gracefully.
const createUploadsDir = async () => {
    try {
        await fs.mkdir(uploadsDir, { recursive: true });
    } catch (e) {
        console.error('[ERROR] Could not create uploads directory:', e.message);
        process.exit(1);
    }
};
createUploadsDir();

// Multer configuration for file uploads. Files are stored in memory (multer.memoryStorage())
// and then written to disk in the route handler to ensure unique naming.
const upload = multer({
    storage: multer.memoryStorage(),
    limits: { fileSize: 100 * 1024 * 1024, files: 10 }, // 100MB file size, max 10 files
    fileFilter: (_req, file, cb) => {
        const allowedTypes = [
            'application/x-executable', 'application/x-msdownload', 'application/x-sharedlib',
            'application/octet-stream', 'application/x-dll', 'application/x-exe',
            'application/x-elf', 'application/x-mach-o'
        ];
        const allowedExtensions = ['.exe', '.dll', '.elf', '.bin', '.scr', '.cpl', '.dylib', '.so'];
        const fileExtension = path.extname(file.originalname).toLowerCase();
        const isAllowed = allowedTypes.includes(file.mimetype) || allowedExtensions.includes(fileExtension);
        cb(isAllowed ? null : new Error(File type not supported: ${file.mimetype}), isAllowed);
    }
});

// Rate limiting middleware to protect API endpoints.
const apiLimiter = rateLimit({
    windowMs: 15 * 60 * 1000, // 15 minutes
    max: 100, // Max 100 requests per 15 minutes
    message: "Too many requests from this IP, please try again after 15 minutes."
});

// Rate limit for file uploads (optional, but recommended)
const uploadLimiter = rateLimit({
    windowMs: 15 * 60 * 1000, // 15 minutes
    max: 20, // Max 20 uploads per 15 minutes
    message: "Too many uploads from this IP, please try again after 15 minutes."
});

// CORS options, supporting a specific origin or allowing all in a controlled manner.
const corsOptions = {
    origin: (origin, callback) => {
        const allowedOrigin = process.env.ALLOWED_ORIGIN || '*'; // Default to '*' for dev, specify for prod
        if (allowedOrigin === '*' || origin === allowedOrigin) {
            callback(null, true);
        } else {
            callback(new Error('Not allowed by CORS'));
        }
    }
};

// Middleware to require authentication via Authorization header or query parameter.
const requireAuth = (req, res, next) => {
    if (!authToken) return next(); // If no token is set, authentication is bypassed (dev only)
    const token = req.headers['authorization']?.split(' ')[1] || req.query.token;
    return token === authToken ? next() : res.status(401).json({ error: 'Unauthorized' });
};

// Global error handler for centralized error management.
const errorHandler = (err, _req, res, _next) => {
    console.error('[Unhandled Error]', err.stack || err.message);
    res.status(500).json({ error: 'Internal Server Error' });
};

// File cleanup cron job, running daily at midnight to delete files older than 24 hours.
cron.schedule('0 0 * * *', async () => {
    console.log('Running scheduled file cleanup...');
    const now = Date.now();
    const oneDayInMs = 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000;
    try {
        const files = await fs.readdir(uploadsDir);
        for (const file of files) {
            const filePath = path.join(uploadsDir, file);
            const stats = await fs.stat(filePath);
            if ((now - stats.mtime.getTime()) > oneDayInMs) {
                await fs.unlink(filePath);
                console.log(Deleted old file: ${file});
            }
        }
        console.log('File cleanup completed.');
    } catch (e) {
        console.error('File cleanup failed:', e.message);
    }
});

// --- Main Application Configuration ---
// Configure Helmet for stricter security headers
app.use(helmet({
    contentSecurityPolicy: {
        directives: {
            defaultSrc: ["'self'"],
            scriptSrc: ["'self'", "'unsafe-inline'"], // Adjust as needed for your front-end scripts
            objectSrc: ["'none'"],
            // Add other directives as required by your application
        },
    },
    noSniff: true,
    xssFilter: true,
}));
app.use(cors(corsOptions)); // CORS configuration
app.use(express.json({ limit: '1mb' })); // Body parsing for JSON requests
app.use(morgan('combined')); // Request logging
app.use('/static', express.static(path.join(__dirname, 'public'))); // Serve static files from 'public'
app.use('/api/', apiLimiter); // Apply rate limiting to API routes

// Asynchronously initialize core engine modules.
(async () => {
    try {
        await rawrzEngine.initializeModules();
        console.log('[OK] RawrZ core engine initialized');
    } catch (e) {
        console.error('[WARN] Core engine init failed:', e.message);
    }
})();

// --- API Route Definitions ---

// Allowlisted cryptographic algorithms for validation.
const allowedAlgorithms = ['sha256', 'sha512', 'aes-256-gcm', 'aes-128-cbc'];

const checkAlgorithm = (algorithm, res) => {
    if (!allowedAlgorithms.includes(algorithm?.toLowerCase())) {
        res.status(400).json({ error: 'Unsupported algorithm' });
        return true;
    }
    return false;
};

// Create a separate router for crypto endpoints with a smaller body limit.
const cryptoRouter = express.Router();
cryptoRouter.use(express.json({ limit: '64kb' })); // Cap crypto routes to 64kb
app.use('/api/hash', requireAuth, cryptoRouter);
app.use('/api/encrypt', requireAuth, cryptoRouter);
app.use('/api/decrypt', requireAuth, cryptoRouter);


// Basic routes.
app.get('/health', (_req, res) => res.json({ ok: true, status: 'healthy' }));
app.get('/panel', (_req, res) => res.sendFile(path.join(__dirname, 'public', 'panel.html')));
app.get('/', (_req, res) => res.redirect('/panel'));

// Cryptographic API endpoints.
app.post('/api/hash', requireAuth, body('input').isString().notEmpty(), async (req, res) => {
    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });
    try {
        const { input, algorithm = 'sha256', save = false, extension } = req.body;
        if (checkAlgorithm(algorithm, res)) return;
        res.json(await rawrz.hash(input, algorithm, !!save, extension));
    } catch (e) {
        res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
    }
});

app.post('/api/encrypt', requireAuth, body('input').isString().notEmpty(), body('algorithm').isString().notEmpty(), async (req, res) => {
    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });
    try {
        const { algorithm, input, extension } = req.body;
        if (checkAlgorithm(algorithm, res)) return;
        res.json(await rawrz.encrypt(algorithm, input, extension));
    } catch (e) {
        res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
    }
});

app.post('/api/decrypt', requireAuth, body('input').isString().notEmpty(), body('algorithm').isString().notEmpty(), async (req, res) => {
    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });
    try {
        const { algorithm, input, key, iv, extension } = req.body;
        if (checkAlgorithm(algorithm, res)) return;
        res.json(await rawrz.decrypt(algorithm, input, key, iv, extension));
    } catch (e) {
        res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
    }
});

// Network-related API endpoints.
app.get('/api/dns', requireAuth, query('hostname').isString().notEmpty(), async (req, res) => {
    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });
    try {
        res.json(await rawrz.dnsLookup(String(req.query.hostname)));
    } catch (e) {
        res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
    }
});

app.get('/api/ping', requireAuth, query('host').isString().notEmpty(), async (req, res) => {
    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });
    try {
        res.json(await rawrz.ping(String(req.query.host), false));
    } catch (e) {
        res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
    }
});

// File management API endpoints.
app.get('/api/files', requireAuth, async (_req, res) => {
    try {
        const filenames = (await fs.readdir(uploadsDir)).filter(file => file !== '.gitkeep');
        res.json(filenames);
    } catch (e) {
        res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
    }
});

app.post('/api/upload', requireAuth, uploadLimiter, upload.single('file'), async (req, res) => {
    if (!req.file) {
        return res.status(400).json({ success: false, error: 'No file uploaded' });
    }

    try {
        const uniqueSuffix = crypto.randomBytes(16).toString('hex');
        const filename = ${uniqueSuffix}-${req.file.originalname};
        const filePath = path.join(uploadsDir, filename);

        await fs.writeFile(filePath, req.file.buffer);
        await fs.chmod(filePath, 0o600); // Set file permissions to readable/writable only by owner

        res.json({
            success: true,
            originalName: req.file.originalname,
            uploadedName: filename,
            size: req.file.size,
            mimetype: req.file.mimetype,
            message: 'File uploaded successfully'
        });
    } catch (error) {
        console.error('Upload error:', error);
        res.status(500).json({ success: false, error: error.message });
    }
});

app.get('/api/download', requireAuth, query('filename').isString().notEmpty().customSanitizer(value => path.basename(value)), async (req, res) => {
    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });
    try {
        const filename = req.query.filename;
        const filePath = path.join(uploadsDir, filename);
        
        // Ensure path is within the uploads directory and exists, preventing path traversal
        if (!filePath.startsWith(uploadsDir)) {
            return res.status(403).json({ error: 'Access denied' });
        }
        await fs.access(filePath, fs.constants.F_OK);

        res.download(filePath, filename);
    } catch (e) {
        res.status(404).json({ error: 'File not found' });
    }
});

app.post('/api/encrypt-file', requireAuth, upload.single('file'), async (req, res) => {
    if (!req.file) {
        return res.status(400).json({ success: false, error: 'No file uploaded' });
    }
    try {
        const algorithm = req.body.algorithm || 'aes-256-gcm';
        const outputFormat = req.body.outputFormat || 'enc';
        
        if (checkAlgorithm(algorithm, res)) return;
        
        const result = await rawrz.encrypt(algorithm, req.file.buffer.toString('base64'), outputFormat);
        
        res.json({
            success: true,
            originalName: req.file.originalname,
            algorithm: algorithm,
            size: req.file.size,
            result: result
        });
    } catch (error) {
        console.error('Encryption error:', error);
        res.status(500).json({ success: false, error: error.message });
    }
});

// Panel navigation routes.
app.get('/rawrz-panels/encrypt', (_req, res) => 
    res.sendFile(path.join(__dirname, 'public', 'encryption-panel.html'))
);

app.get('/encryptor', (_req, res) => 
    res.sendFile(path.join(__dirname, 'public', 'encryption-panel.html'))
);

// Engine status endpoint.
app.get('/api/engines', requireAuth, async (req, res) => {
    try {
        const result = await rawrzEngine.getEngineStatuses();
        res.json({ engines: result, status: 'loaded' });
    } catch (e) {
        res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
    }
});

// Global error handler must be the last middleware added.
app.use(errorHandler);

// Start the server.
const port = parseInt(process.env.PORT || '8080', 10);
app.listen(port, () => console.log([OK] RawrZ HTTP Platform listening on port ${port}));
ChatGPT said:

Thought for 14s
rawr, this is tight—just a few high-impact nits to make it bulletproof. Here are surgical, copy-paste fixes (kept tiny, no churn):

1) Fix fs.promises vs fs.constants
Right now you import only promises, but later call fs.constants.F_OK (undefined). Split sync vs promises.

// replace this:
const fs = require('fs').promises;

// with this:
const fssync = require('fs');
const fs = fssync.promises;
And in your download route change:

await fs.access(filePath, fssync.constants.F_OK);
2) Resolve + guard download path (stronger traversal defense)
Use absolute resolution and guard against prefix tricks. Also reuse a precomputed root.

// add once near your other consts
const resolvedUploadsRoot = path.resolve(uploadsDir) + path.sep;

// replace your /api/download handler with this:
app.get(
  '/api/download',
  requireAuth,
  query('filename').isString().notEmpty().customSanitizer(v => path.basename(String(v))),
  async (req, res) => {
    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });

    const fileName = path.basename(String(req.query.filename));
    const safePath = path.resolve(uploadsDir, fileName);

    if (!safePath.startsWith(resolvedUploadsRoot)) {
      return res.status(403).json({ error: 'Access denied' });
    }
    try {
      await fs.access(safePath, fssync.constants.F_OK);
      return res.download(safePath, fileName);
    } catch {
      return res.status(404).json({ error: 'File not found' });
    }
  }
);
3) Sanitize uploaded filename (strip paths)
Prevents weird names from smuggling slashes/backslashes.

// in /api/upload, change how you build filename:
const base = path.basename(req.file.originalname || 'file');
const filename = `${crypto.randomBytes(16).toString('hex')}-${base}`;
const filePath = path.join(uploadsDir, filename);

await fs.writeFile(filePath, req.file.buffer);
await fs.chmod(filePath, 0o600);
4) Helmet options: remove deprecated xssFilter
xssFilter was removed from Helmet; it’s a no-op now. Keep CSP and nosniff (good!), but drop xssFilter.

app.use(helmet({
  contentSecurityPolicy: {
    directives: {
      defaultSrc: ["'self'"],
      scriptSrc: ["'self'", "'unsafe-inline'"], // drop 'unsafe-inline' in prod if possible
      objectSrc: ["'none'"],
      imgSrc: ["'self'", "data:"],
      connectSrc: ["'self'"],
    },
  },
  noSniff: true,
}));
5) Crypto body size cap: apply middleware directly on the three routes
Your cryptoRouter is mounted but the routes are defined on app, which is fine, but simpler and clearer is per-route caps. Remove the three app.use('/api/...', requireAuth, cryptoRouter); lines, then:

const cryptoJson = express.json({ limit: '64kb' });

// Hash
app.post('/api/hash',
  requireAuth,
  cryptoJson,
  body('input').isString().notEmpty(),
  async (req, res) => { /* unchanged handler */ }
);

// Encrypt
app.post('/api/encrypt',
  requireAuth,
  cryptoJson,
  body('input').isString().notEmpty(),
  body('algorithm').isString().notEmpty(),
  async (req, res) => { /* unchanged handler */ }
);

// Decrypt
app.post('/api/decrypt',
  requireAuth,
  cryptoJson,
  body('input').isString().notEmpty(),
  body('algorithm').isString().notEmpty(),
  async (req, res) => { /* unchanged handler */ }
);
6) Don’t redeclare port
You declare port at the top and again at the bottom. Keep one. Easiest: keep the top one and change the bottom to:

app.listen(port, () =>
  console.log(`[OK] RawrZ HTTP Platform listening on port ${port}`)
);
Why these matter (quick brain dump)
fssync.constants: without it, fs.constants.F_OK throws, breaking downloads.

Path resolution guard: path.resolve + strict startsWith(root + sep) shuts down traversal edge cases.

basename on upload: avoids “C:\path\evil.exe” turning into nested directories on some platforms.

Helmet cleanup: no dead options; CSP + nosniff do the heavy lifting.

64 KB JSON cap (per-route): kills the heap-balloon DoS on crypto routes without affecting others.

Single port: no shadowing or accidental mismatch.

If you want to push this one notch further next: switch to opaque file IDs for downloads (ID → filename map) and return signed, short-lived links. Still compact, but it makes guessing filenames useless.

        res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
    }
});

    try {
        // Read directory and filter out the '.gitkeep' file

        res.json(filenames);
    } catch (e) {
        console.error('Error listing files:', e.message);
        res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
    }

    if (!req.file) {
        return res.status(400).json({ error: 'No file uploaded or file type not supported.' });
    }

    // Generate a unique filename to prevent collisions and potential security issues.
    const uniqueFilename = ${Date.now()}-${crypto.randomBytes(8).toString('hex')}-${originalname};

        // Write the file from memory to the designated uploads directory.

    } catch (error) {
        console.error('File upload error:', error);
        res.status(500).json({ error: 'Failed to save the file.' });
    }
});

    const assignedPort = server.address().port;
    console.log(Server is running on port ${assignedPort});
});

Thought for 6s
rawr, you’re 98% there. Here are tiny, copy-paste patches to land it cleanly and close the remaining security gotchas.

1) Fix fs.promises vs fs.constants
You call fs.constants later, but you only imported promises. Split sync vs promises:

// replace this:
const fs = require('fs').promises;

// with this:
const fssync = require('fs');
const fs = fssync.promises;
Whenever you check existence, use:

await fs.access(safePath, fssync.constants.F_OK);
2) Safe download route (LFI/path traversal closed)
Add this once near your file routes:

// strict inside-uploads guard using absolute paths
const resolvedUploadsRoot = path.resolve(uploadsDir) + path.sep;

app.get(
  '/api/download',
  requireAuth,
  query('filename').isString().notEmpty().customSanitizer(v => path.basename(String(v))),
  async (req, res) => {
    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });

    const fileName = path.basename(String(req.query.filename));
    const safePath = path.resolve(uploadsDir, fileName);

    if (!safePath.startsWith(resolvedUploadsRoot)) {
      return res.status(403).json({ error: 'Access denied' });
    }
    try {
      await fs.access(safePath, fssync.constants.F_OK);
      return res.download(safePath, fileName);
    } catch {
      return res.status(404).json({ error: 'File not found' });
    }
  }
);
3) Sanitize uploaded filename + de-exec on disk
Harden your upload handler with basename and chmod:

// before building uniqueFilename:
const base = path.basename(originalname || 'file');
const uniqueFilename = `${Date.now()}-${crypto.randomBytes(8).toString('hex')}-${base}`;
const filePath = path.join(uploadsDir, uniqueFilename);

// after write:
await fs.writeFile(filePath, buffer);
await fs.chmod(filePath, 0o600); // owner read/write only (POSIX-safe)
4) Helmet: remove deprecated xssFilter
xssFilter is deprecated/no-op in modern Helmet. Keep CSP + nosniff:

app.use(helmet({
  contentSecurityPolicy: {
    directives: {
      defaultSrc: ["'self'"],
      scriptSrc: ["'self'", "'unsafe-inline'"], // drop 'unsafe-inline' in prod if possible
      objectSrc: ["'none'"],
      imgSrc: ["'self'", "data:"],
      connectSrc: ["'self'"],
    },
  },
  noSniff: true,
}));
5) (Nice to have) Rate limiting works best behind proxies
If you’re behind a load balancer/CDN, add this once so rateLimit sees the real client IP:

app.set('trust proxy', 1);
That’s it. With these tiny edits, you’ve got:

Traversal-proof downloads ✅

No accidental exec bits on uploads ✅

Correct fs.constants usage ✅

Helmet config that actually applies ✅

Clean, per-route crypto body limits (already in your cryptoRouter) ✅

Next micro-upgrade when you’re ready: switch downloads to opaque IDs (ID → filename map) and return short-lived HMAC-signed links. Still compact, but it makes guessing filenames a non-starter.

    const token = process.env.AUTH_TOKEN || crypto.randomBytes(32).toString('hex');
    if (!process.env.AUTH_TOKEN) {
        console.warn([WARN] No AUTH_TOKEN found in environment. A new, temporary token has been generated.
          This will change on restart. Use the token below for authenticated routes:);
        console.log([INFO] Current session AUTH_TOKEN: ${token});

    return token;

        await fs.mkdir(uploadsDir, { recursive: true });
    } catch (e) {
        console.error('[ERROR] Could not create uploads directory:', e.message);
        process.exit(1);
    }
};
createUploadsDir();

// Multer configuration for file uploads. Files are stored in memory (multer.memoryStorage())
// and then written to disk in the route handler to ensure unique naming.
const upload = multer({
    storage: multer.memoryStorage(),
    limits: { fileSize: 100 * 1024 * 1024, files: 10 }, // 100MB file size, max 10 files
    fileFilter: (_req, file, cb) => {
        const allowedTypes = [
            'application/x-executable', 'application/x-msdownload', 'application/x-sharedlib',
            'application/octet-stream', 'application/x-dll', 'application/x-exe',
            'application/x-elf', 'application/x-mach-o'
        ];
        const allowedExtensions = ['.exe', '.dll', '.elf', '.bin', '.scr', '.cpl', '.dylib', '.so'];
        const fileExtension = path.extname(file.originalname).toLowerCase();
        const isAllowed = allowedTypes.includes(file.mimetype) || allowedExtensions.includes(fileExtension);
        cb(isAllowed ? null : new Error(File type not supported: ${file.mimetype}), isAllowed);
    }
});

// Rate limiting middleware to protect API endpoints.
const apiLimiter = rateLimit({
    windowMs: 15 * 60 * 1000, // 15 minutes
    max: 100, // Max 100 requests per 15 minutes
    message: "Too many requests from this IP, please try again after 15 minutes."
});

// Rate limit for file uploads (optional, but recommended)
const uploadLimiter = rateLimit({
    windowMs: 15 * 60 * 1000, // 15 minutes
    max: 20, // Max 20 uploads per 15 minutes
    message: "Too many uploads from this IP, please try again after 15 minutes."
});

// CORS options, supporting a specific origin or allowing all in a controlled manner.
const corsOptions = {
    origin: (origin, callback) => {
        const allowedOrigin = process.env.ALLOWED_ORIGIN || '*'; // Default to '*' for dev, specify for prod
        if (allowedOrigin === '*' || origin === allowedOrigin) {
            callback(null, true);
        } else {
            callback(new Error('Not allowed by CORS'));
        }
    }
};

// Middleware to require authentication via Authorization header or query parameter.
const requireAuth = (req, res, next) => {
    if (!authToken) return next(); // If no token is set, authentication is bypassed (dev only)
    const token = req.headers['authorization']?.split(' ')[1] || req.query.token;
    return token === authToken ? next() : res.status(401).json({ error: 'Unauthorized' });
};

// Global error handler for centralized error management.
const errorHandler = (err, _req, res, _next) => {
    console.error('[Unhandled Error]', err.stack || err.message);
    res.status(500).json({ error: 'Internal Server Error' });
};

// File cleanup cron job, running daily at midnight to delete files older than 24 hours.
cron.schedule('0 0 * * *', async () => {
    console.log('Running scheduled file cleanup...');
    const now = Date.now();
    const oneDayInMs = 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000;
    try {
        const files = await fs.readdir(uploadsDir);
        for (const file of files) {
            const filePath = path.join(uploadsDir, file);
            const stats = await fs.stat(filePath);
            if ((now - stats.mtime.getTime()) > oneDayInMs) {
                await fs.unlink(filePath);
                console.log(Deleted old file: ${file});
            }
        }
        console.log('File cleanup completed.');
    } catch (e) {
        console.error('File cleanup failed:', e.message);

        directives: {
            defaultSrc: ["'self'"],
            scriptSrc: ["'self'", "'unsafe-inline'"], // Adjust as needed for your front-end scripts
            objectSrc: ["'none'"],
        },
    },
    noSniff: true,
    xssFilter: true,

// Allowlisted cryptographic algorithms for validation.
const allowedAlgorithms = ['sha256', 'sha512', 'aes-256-gcm', 'aes-128-cbc'];

const checkAlgorithm = (algorithm, res) => {
    if (!allowedAlgorithms.includes(algorithm?.toLowerCase())) {
        res.status(400).json({ error: 'Unsupported algorithm' });
        return true;
    }
    return false;

cryptoRouter.post('/hash', body('input').isString().notEmpty(), async (req, res) => {
    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });
    try {
        const { input, algorithm = 'sha256', save = false, extension } = req.body;
        if (checkAlgorithm(algorithm, res)) return;
        res.json(await rawrz.hash(input, algorithm, !!save, extension));
    } catch (e) {
        res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
    }
});

    try {
        const { algorithm, input, extension } = req.body;
        if (checkAlgorithm(algorithm, res)) return;
        res.json(await rawrz.encrypt(algorithm, input, extension));
    } catch (e) {
        res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
    }
});

    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });

        const { algorithm, input, key, iv, extension } = req.body;
        if (checkAlgorithm(algorithm, res)) return;

    } catch (e) {
        res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
    }

        res.json(filenames);
    } catch (e) {
        res.status(500).json({ error: e.message });
    }
});

app.post('/api/upload', requireAuth, uploadLimiter, upload.single('file'), async (req, res) => {
    if (!req.file) {
        return res.status(400).json({ success: false, error: 'No file uploaded' });
    }

    try {
        const uniqueSuffix = crypto.randomBytes(16).toString('hex');
        const filename = ${uniqueSuffix}-${req.file.originalname};
        const filePath = path.join(uploadsDir, filename);

        await fs.writeFile(filePath, req.file.buffer);
        await fs.chmod(filePath, 0o600); // Set file permissions to readable/writable only by owner

        res.json({
            success: true,
            originalName: req.file.originalname,
            uploadedName: filename,
            size: req.file.size,
            mimetype: req.file.mimetype,
            message: 'File uploaded successfully'
        });
    } catch (error) {
        console.error('Upload error:', error);
        res.status(500).json({ success: false, error: error.message });
    }
});

app.get('/api/download', requireAuth, query('filename').isString().notEmpty().customSanitizer(value => path.basename(value)), async (req, res) => {
    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });
    try {
        const filename = req.query.filename;
        const filePath = path.join(uploadsDir, filename);
        
        // Ensure path is within the uploads directory and exists, preventing path traversal
        if (!filePath.startsWith(uploadsDir)) {
            return res.status(403).json({ error: 'Access denied' });
        }
        await fs.access(filePath, fs.constants.F_OK);

        res.download(filePath, filename);
    } catch (e) {
        res.status(404).json({ error: 'File not found' });
    }
});

app.post('/api/encrypt-file', requireAuth, upload.single('file'), async (req, res) => {
    if (!req.file) {
        return res.status(400).json({ success: false, error: 'No file uploaded' });
    }
    try {
        const algorithm = req.body.algorithm || 'aes-256-gcm';
        const outputFormat = req.body.outputFormat || 'enc';
        
        if (checkAlgorithm(algorithm, res)) return;
        
        const result = await rawrz.encrypt(algorithm, req.file.buffer.toString('base64'), outputFormat);
        
        res.json({
            success: true,
            originalName: req.file.originalname,
            algorithm: algorithm,
            size: req.file.size,
            result: result
        });
    } catch (error) {
        console.error('Encryption error:', error);
        res.status(500).json({ success: false, error: error.message });
    }
});

Thought for 8s
rawr, crispy clean! You’re inches from “ship-it.” Here are tiny, copy-paste fixes to make this iteration airtight—no behavior changes, just correctness + hardening.

1) Fix fs.promises vs fs.constants
You call fs.constants.F_OK later, but you only imported promises. Split sync vs promises.

// replace this:
const fs = require('fs').promises;

// with this:
const fssync = require('fs');
const fs = fssync.promises;
Then update your download existence check:

await fs.access(filePath, fssync.constants.F_OK);
2) Strong path traversal guard on download
Use absolute resolution and a precomputed root. Your current startsWith(uploadsDir) can be tricked; fix it like this:

// add once near other consts
const resolvedUploadsRoot = path.resolve(uploadsDir) + path.sep;

// replace your /api/download with:
app.get(
  '/api/download',
  requireAuth,
  query('filename').isString().notEmpty().customSanitizer(v => path.basename(String(v))),
  async (req, res) => {
    const errors = validationResult(req);
    if (!errors.isEmpty()) return res.status(400).json({ errors: errors.array() });

    const fileName = path.basename(String(req.query.filename));
    const filePath = path.resolve(uploadsDir, fileName);

    if (!filePath.startsWith(resolvedUploadsRoot)) {
      return res.status(403).json({ error: 'Access denied' });
    }
    try {
      await fs.access(filePath, fssync.constants.F_OK);
      return res.download(filePath, fileName);
    } catch {
      return res.status(404).json({ error: 'File not found' });
    }
  }
);
3) Sanitize uploaded filename + drop exec bits
Strip any sneaky path components and lock file perms:

// in /api/upload before building the filename:
const base = path.basename(req.file.originalname || 'file');
const filename = `${crypto.randomBytes(16).toString('hex')}-${base}`;
const filePath = path.join(uploadsDir, filename);

// after write:
await fs.writeFile(filePath, req.file.buffer);
await fs.chmod(filePath, 0o600); // owner read/write only (POSIX; harmless on Windows)
4) Helmet: remove deprecated xssFilter
xssFilter is deprecated in Helmet v5+. Keep CSP + nosniff (already great):

app.use(helmet({
  contentSecurityPolicy: {
    directives: {
      defaultSrc: ["'self'"],
      scriptSrc: ["'self'", "'unsafe-inline'"], // drop 'unsafe-inline' in prod if you can
      objectSrc: ["'none'"],
      imgSrc: ["'self'", "data:"],
      connectSrc: ["'self'"],
    },
  },
  noSniff: true,
}));
5) Don’t redeclare port
You declare port at the top and again at the bottom. Keep the top one; change the bottom to:

app.listen(port, () => console.log(`[OK] RawrZ HTTP Platform listening on port ${port}`));
6) (Nice-to-have) Rate limiting accuracy behind proxies
If you’re behind a load balancer/CDN, add:

app.set('trust proxy', 1);
Why this matters
fssync.constants prevents a runtime crash in /api/download.

Absolute path guard shuts down edge-case traversal attempts.

basename on upload avoids path smuggling via originalname.

No xssFilter avoids dead config; CSP + nosniff do the real work.

Single port avoids accidental shadowing.

When you’re ready for the next micro-upgrade, I can add opaque IDs + short-lived HMAC for downloads so filenames aren’t even guessable—still compact, still copy-paste.
